<div id="review_291851064" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/291851064" />
    <a title="Gitte TotallyBookedBlog" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7379751-gitte-totallybookedblog"><img alt="Gitte TotallyBookedBlog" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514886578p2/7379751.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/291851064?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gitte TotallyBookedBlog" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gitte TotallyBookedBlog" href="/user/show/7379751-gitte-totallybookedblog">Gitte TotallyBookedBlog</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer291851064" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2891187460974150373">So I have had this book on my tbr since reading "Unsticky" by the same author. I finally got round to it and I have to say I really liked it. It was NOTHING like Unsticky (which is one of my fave's this year so far) so in a way I was really disappointed in that!! However, seeing as I am not a real fan of chick lit, I've got to say this is the best book I've ever read in that genre. It was REAL, it was FUNNY, and I could RELATE!!!! <br/><br/>The story was so well written. I completely got the issues gettin</span>
  <span id="freeText2891187460974150373" style="display:none">So I have had this book on my tbr since reading "Unsticky" by the same author. I finally got round to it and I have to say I really liked it. It was NOTHING like Unsticky (which is one of my fave's this year so far) so in a way I was really disappointed in that!! However, seeing as I am not a real fan of chick lit, I've got to say this is the best book I've ever read in that genre. It was REAL, it was FUNNY, and I could RELATE!!!! <br /><br />The story was so well written. I completely got the issues getting over what happened during childhood/teenage years/issues with body image and self-esteem...and the need to find that special one. This book is a journey of someone who wants to be noticed not only for who she is but for her perseverance and her journey of pulling herself out of the shadows to the light by learning to LOVE herself AND letting others LOVE her. <br /><br />This story is about sweet, innocent, self-doubting and body conscious Neve. She is a very intelligent and focused girl. Neve has always had issues with food. She became extremely over weight and this marred her for years. She has been in love with William since University but unfortunately he moved to LA and has been gone for 3 years. When William left for LA, Neve decided that she was going to loose all the excess weight so that by the time William came back he would fall in love with her and find her irresistible.<br /><br />After a couple of years Neve is almost at her target weight but a new problem crops up. Neve is completely inexperienced when it comes to men! Her sister Celia takes it upon herself to rectify this by taking her out on "pulling nights" trying to set her up with her work colleagues...this is where we meet Max (who is *sigh* completely YUMMY HOT!!)!!!! I LOVED Max...how could you not!!! Max works with Celia and is a serial flirt!! <br /><br />Max and Neve are complete opposites, they are Night and Day!! It should never work....not even a "pancake relationship" LOL..loved the analogy so won't spoil this one!! This is where I was absolutely HOOKED!!! The interaction between Neve and Max is HILARIOUS, SWEET, YUMMY, and HEART-WRENCHING!!! Ultimately they bring out the best in each other during their time together, however neither of them are perfect. Max is hiding a ton of issues behind his "male-slut" persona and Neve, well I don't even know where to start with her. There were times where I wanted to throw my kindle at the wall and shout at her to stop putting herself down and enough of the weight obsessing already, but Rome wasn't built in one day and neither is self-esteem!! That being said I was totally in tune with Max getting more and more annoyed and irritated with Neve!!<br /><br />I really liked the other characters in the story too (except for William YUK!!)and the other running story lines only added to Neve and Max's journey. One being the bullying tension between Neve and her sister-in-law Charlotte, this one kind of cemented why I felt sorry for Neve rather than jump to the easy option of hating Neve's character for her obsessive self-doubts!!<br /><br />I have a feeling this is a book you will either love or dislike depending on how you feel about Neve. I have no doubt that Max will win everyone over cause he is totally scrumptious...but Neve..well I'll let you decide but I loved her!!!<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2891187460974150373" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_628613901" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/628613901" />
    <a title="Katherine Kouklinou" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9965212-katherine-kouklinou"><img alt="Katherine Kouklinou" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550500710p2/9965212.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/628613901?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katherine Kouklinou" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katherine Kouklinou" href="/user/show/9965212-katherine-kouklinou">Katherine Kouklinou</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780552165402" href="/book/show/10380816-you-don-t-have-to-say-you-love-me">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9965212-katherine-kouklinou?shelf=best-of-the-best">best-of-the-best</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9965212-katherine-kouklinou?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9965212-katherine-kouklinou?shelf=gorgeous-cover-books">gorgeous-cover-books</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9965212-katherine-kouklinou?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer628613901" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8915539729899569620"><b>5+ stars (and much more)</b><br/><br/>I wouldn't be able to express my feeling about this book even if i was talking about it for hours! I LOVED THIS BOOK! After finishing it i realize even more how in love i am with it. If i could date a book, this particular one would be my current companion!<br/><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1376399166p8/824889.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Neve and Max.... Max and Neve... How could it possibly true that two people so different would make a perfect couple?   <span id="freeText8915539729899569620" style="display:none"><b>5+ stars (and much more)</b><br><br>I wouldn't be able to express my feeling about this book even if i was talking about it for hours! I LOVED THIS BOOK! After finishing it i realize even more how in love i am with it. If i could date a book, this particular one would be my current companion!<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1376399166p8/824889.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Neve and Max.... Max and Neve... How could it possibly true that two people so different would make a perfect couple? Is it possible?<br>Without hesitation i say "it is!".<br>Max is sexy, handsome and full with experiences. Neve is sweet, bookish and obsessed with her weight!<br>She believes she can get William (her one "true love") if she was size ten. But then Max comes in her life and turns everything upside down.<br><br><b>“The thing about love was that it caught you unawares, turned up in the most unexpected places, even when you weren't looking for it.”</b> <br><br>He is the one to prove her that she is a special girl and she is more pretty than she thinks!<br>He cares for her, he tease her, he makes her laugh and he is the only boy with the power to make her feel comfortable with herself.<br><br><b>“What you look like is just one part of who you are - but it's not all you are.”</b> <br><br>From the time they start spending time together, they become inseparable! They light up each other's days! They make each other laugh so hard and they care more than they could possibly think...<br><br>The love and sex scenes are awesome and passionate and beautiful and real... do i need to carry on? I think we all got the message!! :P<br><br>You Don't Have to Say You Love Me is a book about love when and where you don't expect you would, about believing and loving yourself and falling in love with an amazing boy!! It's a light read with a lot of beautiful messages about life and love... <br><br>I would recommend it to everyone who wants a beautiful and utterly romantic book to fall in love with!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1376399303p8/824892.jpg" width="300" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br> <b>“Each kiss was like biting into the richest darkest chocolate and pausing to savour the taste.”</b> <br><br>Enjoy!!!! :D</span>

<div id="review_391632579" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/391632579" />
    <a title="Nafiza" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2483439-nafiza"><img alt="Nafiza" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529831446p2/2483439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/391632579?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nafiza" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nafiza" href="/user/show/2483439-nafiza">Nafiza</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2483439-nafiza?shelf=read-2012">read-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer391632579" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12193789446542523218">I keep saying that I don’t read chicklit and I don’t but when it comes to Manning, somehow I do. It’s just that her writing style is so engaging. I may have said this before, I probably have in another review of her book and if I have, forgive me, but her writing style is akin to sitting down with a bunch of girlfriends and exchanging the most delicious gossip. There’s something natural, something charming about the tone in which the story is narrated that even the most fantastic circumstances b</span>
  <span id="freeText12193789446542523218" style="display:none">I keep saying that I don’t read chicklit and I don’t but when it comes to Manning, somehow I do. It’s just that her writing style is so engaging. I may have said this before, I probably have in another review of her book and if I have, forgive me, but her writing style is akin to sitting down with a bunch of girlfriends and exchanging the most delicious gossip. There’s something natural, something charming about the tone in which the story is narrated that even the most fantastic circumstances become believable.<br /><br />You Don’t Have to Say You Love Me is about pancake relationships. A pancake relationship, according to Neve Slater is a practice relationship for the real one. Okay, Neve? Girl has many issues, the least of them being her weight. She has worked hard to lose all her weight but it isn’t enough, it won’t be enough until she reaches the magical size ten that will somehow transform her into the goddess that her love in America will see and fall for her. What distinguishes this from the usual fat-girl-slim novel is how realistically Manning narrates this. This is no Cinderella story, guys. Usually, in books that deal with these themes, the author glosses over the process of beautification, she doesn’t discuss what it means to be fat, what it means to be on a diet, the hunger pangs, the very real esteem issues, none of that is considered. In You Don’t Have to Say You Love Me these things are portrayed. The extreme diet, the exercise, the sacrifices, everything is told in a matter of fact tone. And I liked that. I could relate to that! I winced, I cringed, I laughed and I nodded my head.<br /><br />And then there’s the romance. Manning is genius at creating these very swoonworthy love interests who are just so damned flawed but manage to be awesome anyway. There was that older guy in UnSticky and Christopher in Adorkable. Max is no exception. I love that he is fleshed out as a character and that his exchanged and conversations with Neve are less stilted dialogue and more an accurate reflection of what reality could possibly be. Their relationship is full of holes but they fit together. Even when they can’t see it, they do.<br /><br />The ending also convinced me that this book deserves it’s five stars. Neve learns her lessons, about her weight, her worth and about illusion and reality. She learns to love not just herself but the man she didn’t expect to. Do I recommend this? You know, I do. I think this is one hell of a ride and who doesn’t like gossiping with their girlfriends?</span>
  <a data-text-id="12193789446542523218" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6113622613700717106">You know what? Life is too short for shitty books with shitty characters and shitty plots. I started this book with not so high expectations and still was let down. So I'm not going to finish it. <br/><br/>For once, I'd like to read a book about a confident woman. A woman who not only loves her body, but loves her personality and her job. I'm so sick of these self-loathing chicks who are always insecure about belly fat and are frequently surprised when attractive men show them even the slightest bit if in</span>
  <span id="freeText6113622613700717106" style="display:none">You know what? Life is too short for shitty books with shitty characters and shitty plots. I started this book with not so high expectations and still was let down. So I'm not going to finish it. <br /><br />For once, I'd like to read a book about a confident woman. A woman who not only loves her body, but loves her personality and her job. I'm so sick of these self-loathing chicks who are always insecure about belly fat and are frequently surprised when attractive men show them even the slightest bit if interest. It's so pathetic that every female character is sad and disappointed in themselves, surrounded by friends who are seemingly more gorgeous than they are and who are constantly trying to make their life better by finding them a guy to fix their problems.<br /><br />This very much describes Neve. She's highly insecure and has this awful younger sister who is fashionable and thin and she meets this most handsome god named Max who fucks around with models and celebs. Now instead of just appreciating this Adonis, Neve blows her chance to be seduced like a regular woman by thinking about how totally fat and ugly she is.... And this is DURING SEXUAL INTERCOURSE!!!! YES. This man has his glorious holy penis inside her and all she can think about is how impossible it is for a man to even have an erection around her.... <br /><br />Now I would continue reading, just to see where this is going, because right now she's writing him a letter (yes a letter; fountain pen and everything) about why she tensed up like a dead alligator, ruined his stiffy and then told him to leave. But I simply do not have the time. I am tired of these women waiting for a man to convince them that they're beautiful and sexy. Sick and tired.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7619766479371092086"><b> 5++++ Neve and Max Stars Every Time!!!! </b><br/><br/><b> What's it about? </b> A girl with an eating/body image disorder decides to have a temporary relationship with the local heart-breaker to help her prepare for the real thing... <br/><br/><b> The best bit: </b> oh I LOVE this book sooo much. Every couple of years I come back to it and after having read this FOUR TIMES, I still absolutely devour every delectable word. <br/><br/>I love Neve. <br/>I love her job as a literary archivist.<br/>I love her apartment.<br/>I love her self-discipline. <br/>And I love</span>
  <span id="freeText7619766479371092086" style="display:none"><b> 5++++ Neve and Max Stars Every Time!!!! </b><br /><br /><b> What's it about? </b> A girl with an eating/body image disorder decides to have a temporary relationship with the local heart-breaker to help her prepare for the real thing... <br /><br /><b> The best bit: </b> oh I LOVE this book sooo much. Every couple of years I come back to it and after having read this FOUR TIMES, I still absolutely devour every delectable word. <br /><br />I love Neve. <br />I love her job as a literary archivist.<br />I love her apartment.<br />I love her self-discipline. <br />And I love her fitness stamina and endurance.<br />And I even love her commitment to her ideal illusion (that will make more sense once you read it).<br /><br />I love Max and his traumatised dog.<br />I love Max's frayed jeans and his ability to <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ go down on Neve for 30 minutes because he lost at Scrabble which is really his ability to  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> accept defeat.<br />I love his humour and his patience. <br />I love his easy-going nature.<br />I love his eye-rolls and the way he eats strawberries with Neve.<br /><br />I love Sarra Manning's insight into weightloss and body image.<br />I love her pacing and character development.<br />And I love that every female (and male) character in this book differs so thoroughly from eachother.<br /><br /><b> The worst bits: </b> No resolution of Douglas' story, and an absence of heart-swoony declarations. (Okay, these worst bits are also, at the same time, the best bits. Weird, right?) I also wanted one more scene with Gustav.<br /><br /><b> Recommended for: </b> fans of slow burn, faux relationships that turn to romance. The story also focuses on the body image issues that remain after profound weightloss and the obsessive vulnerability of eating disorders.</span>

<div id="review_764843588" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/764843588" />
    <a title="Crazy for Books (Stephanie)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2949869-crazy-for-books-stephanie"><img alt="Crazy for Books (Stephanie)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1426774885p2/2949869.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/764843588?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Crazy for Books (Stephanie)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Crazy for Books (Stephanie)" href="/user/show/2949869-crazy-for-books-stephanie">Crazy for Books (Stephanie)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2949869-crazy-for-books-stephanie?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2949869-crazy-for-books-stephanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2949869-crazy-for-books-stephanie?shelf=funny">funny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2949869-crazy-for-books-stephanie?shelf=borrowed">borrowed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer764843588" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5591238131105384615"><b>4 Stars</b><br/><br/>Neve has spent the last three years going fighting for her life in losing weight to be a sized 10. She's in love with William, whom she met at Oxford, but who has been in California teaching for the past three years. Part of Neve's goal is to look like the woman she believes he will want to spend his life with, not only in mind but in body. The problem is, at 25 years old, Neve has absolutely no experience with relations. She's devised a plan to have what she calls a pancake relations to </span>
  <span id="freeText5591238131105384615" style="display:none"><b>4 Stars</b><br /><br />Neve has spent the last three years going fighting for her life in losing weight to be a sized 10. She's in love with William, whom she met at Oxford, but who has been in California teaching for the past three years. Part of Neve's goal is to look like the woman she believes he will want to spend his life with, not only in mind but in body. The problem is, at 25 years old, Neve has absolutely no experience with relations. She's devised a plan to have what she calls a pancake relations to gain experience, so that when William returns she will be ready to be in the perfect relationship. Enter Max. <br /><br />Max works at the fashion magazine where Neve's sister works. One disastrous meeting with the manwhore that is Max and a failed attempt at sex brings Max into Neve's life as the perfect fake boyfriend. Neve believes she will never want more from him, if he can even stand being with her.<br /><br />What Neve doesn't realize is nothing is perfect. <br /><br />I thought this was a really sweet story. I loved Neve and her complete lack of knowing anything about relationships and what men and women really expect of each other. She was so used to being in the background that she didn't realized that the more you become involved with people the messier relationships become. From misunderstandings to forgiving someone for saying something that crosses a line.<br /><br />I was a bit skeptical of what Max was getting out of their relationship until he revealed why he started dating her, when he never was one known for ever wanting a relationship. Although I loved their interactions and Neve discovering she had more of a backbone than even she realized, the idea that a guy who was consistently around models and celebrities, would choose a girl like Neve no matter how sweet and loving she was, a bit unrealistic. I would hope that things could actually be that way and someone stunning could look past the outside to the inside of a person. But that hasn't been my experience. But it's a nice idea.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5591238131105384615" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_159831921" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/159831921" />
    <a title="Caro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3927155-caro"><img alt="Caro" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/159831921?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caro" href="/user/show/3927155-caro">Caro</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3927155-caro?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer159831921" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9879331893991507494">I read this book a little while ago and Neve's story is still present in my head. Her fight against her weight, but especially against herself, hasn't left me since.<br/><br/>When I think about Chick Lit as a genre, I usually picture a couple of blonde fashionistas going shopping and searching for love in a big city (like probably most of the people who don't actually read Chick Lit). So I tend to dismiss those books very easily - you know, with all those pirates, dragons and werewolves books I haven't re</span>
  <span id="freeText9879331893991507494" style="display:none">I read this book a little while ago and Neve's story is still present in my head. Her fight against her weight, but especially against herself, hasn't left me since.<br /><br />When I think about Chick Lit as a genre, I usually picture a couple of blonde fashionistas going shopping and searching for love in a big city (like probably most of the people who don't actually read Chick Lit). So I tend to dismiss those books very easily - you know, with all those pirates, dragons and werewolves books I haven't read why on earth would I read a Chick Lit book?<br /><br />Well maybe because these books talk about me. Not me me. But me as a person, a woman living in this century (where the existence of dragons and werewolves still hasn't been proven yet). One of the best aspects of the book is how contemporary it feels. Sarra Manning gave Neve's story a context that many people can relate to with themes such as issues to find a decent job, to make friends at work, to get over what happened during your teenage years etc. The atmosphere feels very real and shows how much some people struggle nowadays to find happiness or fulfilment.<br />Neve is a very realistic and striking character. She is very bright and her job might not be thrilling per se but she enjoys it (to a certain extent) and has some hopes of one day publishing a book. She has been in love with William since University and despite his move to LA. Neve had a little problem with food during her teenage years and became overweight. When William left for America, she set herself the goal of losing all her weight and becoming "perfect" so that William, upon his return, would fall in love with her. <br />A couple of years later and many pounds less, Neve thinks she is prepared for William's return but her sister Celia reminds her of the tiny issue of Neve's complete inexperience in men. As in complete inexperience. Enters Celia's mad plan to take Neve to her work (fashion magazine!) party and introduce her to some of her colleagues. Little does she know that womaniser Max will be the one chosen by Neve.<br /><br />The contrast between bookish Neve and ladies' man celebrity journalist Max is striking, but it is what makes their interactions so fascinating. They are worlds' apart in appearance but find some deep-rooted connections. I just love what happened between them as well as being able to see behind the scenes of fashion magazines and the world of celebrities. Sarra Manning - having been a journalist for years - depicts very well this world.<br /><br />The characterisation in the story is just brilliant. I tweeted Sarra Manning about the realism of Neve's personality, and she told me that she drew a lot of her own experience for this book, qualifying it as her most "me" book. You can read her incredible piece for The Telegraph here where she talks about her transformation.<br /><br />But describing You Don't Have To Say You Love Me as a book about weight and diet would be too reductive. The book is a coming-of-age story of someone who has always lived in the shadows and about her journey to learn how to love herself.<br /><br />The explicit sex scenes made me blush down to my toes - note to self: do not read explicit sex scenes in the tube where people read over your shoulder.<br />I loved how all the characters had very distinctive personalities and how they related to Neve: her father, her sister, her brother's wife (and ex-bully when she was at school), her gym trainer and her friends at work. I liked the story of her attempting to write a book on Lucy Keener and how it interestingly completed the main plot.<br /><br />The writing is simply gorgeous. Sarra Manning has amazing story-telling skills and I literally couldn't put the book down.<br /> I really loved this book, I found that the characters and the contemporary-feel of the story was fascinating. It is a feel good book in the most realistic way possible (no irrational makeovers or unbelievable male love interests). If you are a fan of Chick Lit, you will love this book, but you might also like it if you are not a fan of the genre!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9879331893991507494" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('qyvGgdA/oW2Fw9J3KqSvXpKYfjY+SuNJnMwEFsHf2s2QhtVPkZpSOZfy0SMygsqizx5+e5hep6RkokjZ3y9rkQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('AFTzx6Hm0sMUKunAG711w9o6WXaGJVczQgolWwrPxVg7+eAJ4EMhlwYb6pQDmxA/h7xZOyAxE966ZGmUFD90BA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1879748666484126518">Sarra Manning is a teen queen extraordinaire. She spent five years working on the now sadly defunct <i>J17</i>, first as a writer and then as Entertainment Editor. She then joined the launch team of teen fashion bible <i>Ellegirl</i>, which she later went on to edit and has consulted on a wide range of youth titles including Bliss, The Face and More. <br/><br/>Sarra is now editor of <i>What To Wear</i> magazine. She's also been</span>
  <span id="freeText1879748666484126518" style="display:none">Sarra Manning is a teen queen extraordinaire. She spent five years working on the now sadly defunct <i>J17</i>, first as a writer and then as Entertainment Editor. She then joined the launch team of teen fashion bible <i>Ellegirl</i>, which she later went on to edit and has consulted on a wide range of youth titles including Bliss, The Face and More. <br /><br />Sarra is now editor of <i>What To Wear</i> magazine. She's also been a regular contributor to <i>ELLE, The Guardian, ES Magazine, Seventeen, Details</i> and <i>Heat</i> and wrote the Shop Bitch column for <i>Time Out</i>. Sarra lives in North London with her dog Miss Betsy</span>
